Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this operation there is fear that the patient dies immediately, or a fistula results which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the migraine.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of migraine by the methods we have described in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help, then there are three kinds of cautery which are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	One method is that you make three or four cauteries, in a line according to the length of the migraine, according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have described before; and do not press your hand on the whole cautery, and let the patient often lie on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two points, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is at the place of the migraine, or the side of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevations by which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the breadth of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, push the two heated points until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize with the whole cautery with three points.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment, when it has discharged pus for a long time, and this is better than the other treatments mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is of no use for a dropsical person, except in the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in the divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make four cauteries around the belly, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two on the back along the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cautery be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery open to discharge pus for a long time, and do not neglect the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the nail we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what has been shown before.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet.
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in a dropsical person, and are full of yellowish water, you must cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go in too deep, lest the yellowish water be ignited, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make on the two legs two cauteries on each leg at the point of the knife; and let the cauteries be long, one below the knee in front and the other on the outside, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without cleaning, so that the water may escape; afterwards cure it with the other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of the menstruation.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When looseness of the bowels comes from cold and moisture, so that the retentive and digestive power which is in the stomach and in the intestine is weakened, and cannot be cured by other means; and you see the patient is quite strong and of good constitution, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what has been said above about the cautery of the stomach, in a circular cautery; and four small cauteries around the navel with one small, crucial cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each hip, and two small cauteries on the stomach beside the large one, for the cure is profitable when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure of haemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the haemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and are of large, cold, and moist corrupted humours, and are cured as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, those which are quite outside under the armpit little by little in a triangle, and one cautery under the navel two fingers' breadth; and if you think that his stomach is chilled, and the food does not digest, and you see the face swell, then make one large cautery on the stomach, as is said above, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with the crucial cautery; and leave the cautery open a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure, treat the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshy growth which is named "thelul".
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it, burning hot, on the cut thelul; and hold your hand there until the cautery reaches the origin of the vein from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the alchatim, there will be greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of a badly healed wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate incision or opening, which we will describe in its place, such an illness arises that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula occurs in someone, and it is old and discharges pus and corrupt moisture, you should probe it entirely with a thin tent, and ensure that you know completely, using the tent, how deep it is.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Then heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to how far the tent entered, and repeat the cautery until the rotten and corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the extent of the need; and take care not to burn the nerves which are there, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestine, guard against those places, and do not apply the fire except to fleshy areas, and intend that it is not penetrating; afterwards, treat the area until it is healed, and if the area is sealed, and the matter is expelled for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter is not expelled, know that the area is rotten, and the bone at the bottom is corrupt; and thus as one of those that we will describe in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of the illness of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes to the kidneys, and from great flatulence, and he does not desire women, then it is necessary that you cauterize him over the kidneys on one side and the other with the claviform cautery that we have described before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will do greater aid.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make a cautery on the outer part over the bladder, where the hairs of the pubis begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of a thumb; and make one cautery on the outer part of the back, or two if you need it; and let the cautery be claviform according to the form previously described.
de la marris	Of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception because of this, and the flowers (menstruation) are corrupted and their timing is delayed; and when they come, she feels great pain: then it is necessary that three cauteries be made around the buttocks, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries on the outer part of the back; and let the cauteries be claviform, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and because of this it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of the separation is found empty, then you must cauterize the patient over the hip joint with one cautery resembling a circle, and bleed in front of the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like that with which one cauterizes the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available, make three cauteries of the size of an olive, and let the cauteries be as deep as the heart; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment is not effective, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with fetid pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, with burning medicines together, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is done in many ways, of which one is this: that you cauterize on the hip joint three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and wide, and let there be between each cautery a space the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on the head of the hip, so there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the whole hip, and all the thick parts of the flesh are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, make two cauteries where the patient says the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, cauterize where he feels the pain, three or four points with the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a cautery with the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery there so long that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have had cauteries on the ankle of the foot, and they left them there so long that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot also, and the whole foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a bowel movement from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, make a cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said, for the cautery of the hip, of which this is the manner, make one such iron and let the head be as thick as a fingernail, or a little less, and let it be grooved, and let the space between the grooves be from one groove to the other the quantity of a thumb-joint; and let the grooves be open on two sides, and let them be as if knotted, and let there be a well-made iron handle; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and throws off sparks, and then put it on the hip-bone of the diseased hip, and turn it towards the healthy side; and cauterize it once with a round cautery and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open a long time; afterwards treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, for him who can endure it, and where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of burning medicine is that you make an instrument with grooves in which the edge of the door descends, and let it be of bronze or iron with a long wall, and in height it has two knots, and between each has the quantity of the thickness of a finger; and let them be open in front and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place it on the hip-bone of the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand very much on the hip-bone; then pour between the two circles hot water which has been heated a little over the fire, and leave it for one hour, and let the patient endure the heat and burning from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds a burning there like fire; and when the burning is past, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the hip with fresh water, and leave it thus for three days, and put on butter until that which is black from the burn is removed; and leave it for three days so that pus is drawn out; and this would be the final help after treating with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make for him an instrument that holds water according to what you have done to the hip equally; and this is the manner of the hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening such that the point of a razor can enter; and place over that pot another pot well sealed, and put on alkali and lime and fresh water above, until there is two fingers’ depth above the powders when you have well pressed it with your hand; and leave it thus until water descends and drips into the sealed pot, then take all that water, and pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical operations and in cauterizations of other members, for it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one cauterizes the hip well, such as tesisie and honey and anacardi and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of hip pain and sciatica, and praises it greatly, and says that no other cure was done, and that he was healed at one time when this cure was done, and he was bathed as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this manner that you take fresh and dry green litharge, and grind it very finely with a little fat, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours and as much as the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter the bath until his body is somewhat warmed, and make him enter the bed, and the pain will all go away and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cautery with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of humors.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic nerve is cauterized with goat dung, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and put it on the pit that is between the big toe and the other which is called the foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry goat dung, and heat it in the fire until it is coals, and put it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and do it again in the same way, and do not stop doing this until you think by feeling that it reaches down to the hip, and that the pain is ceased; and this kind of cautery is called "goat cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or from percussion or from too great evacuation, or from similar spread cold matter, in none of these cases is cautery of use, except for that which comes from infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient is purged of fetid pills or similar things, that three lines marked with ink be made on his back, where the pain is located, and in each line five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery that is called "points"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries with the middle nail cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the sign of the beginning is that they have shortness of breath when they rise, and fear; and you find in the last spine of the back and in us the appearance which comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, cauterize it with the circular cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery takes each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the pointed cautery two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, cure the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery to a gibbosity which is in a spasm of the nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are from humors that are spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which the physicians properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and medical cures cannot heal it, then it is cured by cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you cauterize on the surface of the foot, make a cautery with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains reach the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make cauteries on each knee, three or four on each side, with the whole olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than until the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have described in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist, two lines; and if some pain remains in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains reach the elbows or the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and you purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the syfac (synovial membrane/tissue)
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the groin, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is recent, then when you wish to cure it, it is necessary that he not eat that day; and that he use things that loosen the bowels, so that the feces descend from his belly; afterward make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his breath while the bowels are replaced, and push them back with your fingers, and make an incision beneath the rupture on the pubic bone, and make a mark similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and emits sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then push the bowels back into place; and the assistant should hold his hand above so that they do not return; and open the patient's thighs well, and place a cushion under him and an assistant on his thighs, and another on his chest to hold his hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bowels do not protrude when you apply the cautery; that you do not burn them; and that thereby the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be small according to their size, and for adults also large according to their size; after three days, treat the site of the cautery with butter until the burn is gone; afterward treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that his diet be light for a long time, so that the bowels do not protrude when he attempts to go to the privy.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage, and let him wear it for forty more days; and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard himself from too great repletion of drink and food, and from too much loud laughter; and when he has followed this instruction, he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will describe the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are noticeable, and you see that they are not growing larger, make a cautery of the round cautery according to its size, and let one-third of the heart be burned; afterward, treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another outside, and hold your hand in the middle with the entire cautery clamped.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, either from a fall or a blow, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then it must be cauterized with the cautery that is called "points," and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and its weakness and its strength and its location of twisting and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on top of that one, for such is the custom that it must move to the limb that is near it, wherefore it is necessary that you make cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of leprosy.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great help, and likewise the illness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see it to be cauterized, take heed if the illness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend or remain, and you fear that the corruption will seize the whole patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head at the nape, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the occiput; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize on the chin according to what is described above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the leprosy is spread everywhere; and it appears manifestly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery on the bridge of the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the rump and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the breasts, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more help you give, and the more it profits; and know that the patient does not feel any pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already all corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you will find in the various types of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, cure the place with barley flour with honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation comes in any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauteries on the limb according to the size of the limb; and let the cauteries penetrate a little into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the inflammation is removed; and however, no one should interfere unless he is knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of albaras (or,  about albaras)
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness which is called "albaras" is chronic, and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a somewhat deep cautery, according to the quantity of the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with barley flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and pigeon blood and swallow blood, of each one part; and let it all be mixed together, and be bound with a cloth, and let air reach the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the edge of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise men say that one should also cauterize the middle of the cancer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen sometimes; and a more straightforward thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery that is called "circular," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot mature.
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness that is called "adubelati," and it delays in maturing either because of the superfluity it produces or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the time; and you wish to hasten its maturation: then cauterize it around with many small, pointed cauteries; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to mature.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it with the whole cautery, then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of that illness which is called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it externally in such a way that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of illness which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a consumption of the limb, for it eats away the limbs like fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then heat the cautery, small and large pins, according to what is necessary for the place where the illness is; afterwards cauterize it on all sides until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places soft bread with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterwards, the cure with ointments that generate flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, that is good; and if not, then begin the cautery again on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this disease is sometimes cured by liquid medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the cure with liquid medicine in the section: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the swellings that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Very often it happens that on the feet, from the outside, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large, foul thing that injures the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is according to two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat a cautery iron as if it were a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron to the measure that it can encompass the nail on all sides, and that it has fine edges; afterward you put it, very hot, on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it thus for three days until it begins to shed pus; then you make a poultice of wild mallows crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with flesh-healing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are inverted [growing inward] beneath the skin, and this often happens in the hands and feet, then you must apply hot water cautery; and it is in this manner: take a chain of bronze or iron, or a goose feather, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is to say, for warts; and place the chain so that it encompasses it entirely, then place a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edges of the chain reach the root of the nail, and the hot water may find a way deep down to the root; and let the patient suffer the bite of the hot water for a little while, for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted completely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have eradicated all those which are on the body, then treat them with ointments which generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other [fevers], then you must make four cauteries or four on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the feet, and one on the stomach with the olive cautery; then the trembling will cease, and the healing of the cold illness will hasten.
des pustules puans	Of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes there appear on the outside of the body boils, or foul pustules, which come from corrupted gross humors.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Then, at the first appearance, you must make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery of myrtle wood, the tip of which is held in the fire, or of the root of aristolochia longa, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed; but this must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great flows of blood from the artery which is cut in a wound that comes from the outside, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And however, when this happens to someone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no drop comes out anymore; then put several small and large olive-shaped cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after another until the blood is stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from the artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied that have the power to stop blood; and it should be tied and pressed tightly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Those who attempt to stop it by tightly binding with cloths or by putting burning things on, or other similar things, will have little success.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a mirror or medicine present, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press well until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but wet it with cold water often, that it be very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and he should do meanwhile what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the treatments of surgery.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the illnesses in which it is necessary to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, and the locations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter in the same way, so that one may more easily find what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, dear son, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first about cauteries, and therefore greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there is often evacuation of blood in opening a vein, and in the incision of an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in the incision of a stone, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die from it.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake anything foolishly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Thus some are so afflicted by their illness that they die easily because of the frenzy they experience from their illness and its severity; and of these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these are some who regain their senses and say, "Wait, I am healed"; and the illness is deceptive.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put greater trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not work foolishly but wisely in that which you are certain of, and from which you can gain both profit and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients to whom salvation may be brought; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and lasting praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and may He inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in sections, according to what precedes in the chapter on cauteries, which I have described to you from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	of the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness very often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife pulls the child's head too hard; and sometimes it comes from a hidden cause that is unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this illness except in children, and in all those whom I have seen, death hastened; and therefore it seems to me that it is better for me to leave the work in such cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled each day until he could not bear it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered under the bone on the dura mater, between the brain and the bone; and the procedure is such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you split open the head with a wide incision; and let it be as long as two fingers, until the moisture flows out; and here is the form of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs that you see are the sutures of the head open on each side, and the water spurts out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this is not hidden from you: then you must make three incisions in the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw all the moisture out.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then dress the incisions with cloths and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it so until the fifth day; then undress it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and give the patient dry meat of little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you observe where the size of the abscess appears, and the collection of the water; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut, then, where the abscess appears, and the collection of water, and cut it according to what power you have; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and a flow of blood comes, so that the patient dies from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of catarrh
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or chest, and the disease is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last treatment is cautery, with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you see them to be cut, that the patient throws back his head; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then the patient constricts his neck with the same cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the place of one and the other is behind the ears, and they are somewhat hidden; then mark the places with ink, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula in two parts, until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the spatula under the artery and cut it above, cutting as with two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not appear to the touch, it is necessary that you measure the amount of space of three fingers, then mark with ink and cut down to the bone; and what is necessary of blood to let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone a point of the membrane, cut it so that no abscess forms, then bind the wound and dress it, and treat with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and old, raging headache and similar things, and it is treated with various kinds of medicinal cures and none of that helps, then we bleed the arteries of the temples and cauterize them there, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient should pull back the hair from his temples, and attend to the artery which appears in the temple, for it appears well by its beating, and is somewhat retracted except in some men who are too cold; and if it is retracted, let the patient bind his neck with some cloths, then rub the place with some rough cloth, and bathe the area with warm water until the artery clearly appears; then take the lancet, of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with forceps, and separate it well from the tissues which are beneath it on each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it with the point of the hook, then cut it from that side according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood does not flow out entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw six ounces of blood, up to three; and if the artery is large, then you must tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread, so that corruption does not come before the healing of the wound, and so that the blood flows; then cut the excess which is between the two ligatures at that very moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a knife cautery down to the bone until the edges are cut; and this is the best operation, if the patient does not have a fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to dry up humors: therefore it is of greater help with humors.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made tents; and when they are untied, it should be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with tents, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you are working, then hasten to cut it with a cautery, or you apply vitriol to the place and press it with your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have that at hand, then put your finger on the place until the blood is congealed, and sprinkle the place with cold water until the blood stops, and it is extracted as necessary; and that which is better and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery from two sides, but the blades should be thick to hold their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two blades one finger's breadth of thickness, and then when you have marked the two places, and you place the burning iron there until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be separated between the two edges because it is not entirely sealed with this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
