Often a disease called "telul" arises at the root of the nose, and grows and becomes large gradually, until it is a frightening sight; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply a cautery or burning medicine to the place; and if one delays cutting it until it is large, take care if it is hard, of a livid color, and insensitive: do not touch it with iron, for it is a cancerous abscess, because when it is cut sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not livid in color, and you see that it can be entirely cut, empty the patient and cut it without fear, and treat the place with drying and astringent things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilaginous structures, it benefits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together in a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must scrape all the parts of their edges until they bleed, then bring the two lips together in a suture, and bind it, and dust on dragon's blood powder, and ground incense; and on top of the powders put a piece of strong plaster or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of suturing is that you bring together the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or with thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In many men, there occurs within the lips a hard abscess, similar to wart grains, both smaller and larger; then you must turn back the lips, and make an incision on each one, and take it with tweezers and cut it in each part; then fill the place after the incision with ground vitriol, until the blood is stopped; and then wash it with vinegar, and treat the place with drying things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there grows on the gums added flesh, which the ancients call "albulus"; then you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run; then put on the place ground vitriol, or other astringent and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and it often happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: it will not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the sordes (or foul matter)
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are gathered at the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, crusts which are foul and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and worm-eaten, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be on your lap, and scrape the teeth where the crusts appear, until nothing remains; and thus do for the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and the other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first scraping, it is good; if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything; and know that the teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demonstrates, because the scrapers with which one scrapes outside the teeth have other forms than those with which one scrapes between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared and with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat a toothache that you delay extraction as long as you can, for one should not do this; for it is a very high operation until one has no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is compelled to extraction, it is necessary that you be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient, and he thinks it is in a sound tooth, and has the good tooth extracted; and yet the pain does not depart for that, until the bad one is extracted, for we have often done this to such sufferers; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to guard the gum on all sides; then move it with your fingers or with fine pliers little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly grasp it with the pliers; and let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards extract the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it inside from each side lightly, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, it is necessary that you fill it with lint where the holes are; and then extract it skillfully with pliers, so that it does not break during extraction; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and that a part remains, and that greater pain than the first returns to the patient through the malice of the root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act as ignorant surgeons do, who through their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw, and do not accomplish what we have recounted; but sometimes bring about through this great illness because of the roots which remain, or because of the jaw which they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the place; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one first moves the teeth should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	Of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you put on the place cotton soaked in butter for one or two days,
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the place is softened, then put there the forceps which are called "algefri", of which the head resembles a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these forceps, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say, a lever, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by this, it is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, of which the shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and of other instruments which are in front in the shape of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large forceps, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise and subtle master finds by himself his instrument, according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of cases; and if one breaks a piece of the cart or other bones, or if it rots, then he looks for the instruments which are necessary, that I have told you, and helps himself with gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then scrape it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural course, and the shape is ugly, and especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth is born after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and one cannot saw or file it: then scrape it; and if it is stuck with the tooth, then take this instrument of which this is the shape, and it is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron, sharp at the top:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little in several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with such a file as this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file with which needles are made; and file the tooth little by little in several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then smooth it at the end with some scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it hurts the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without pain, and you have treated them with astringent medicines, and this is of no use; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, then take the thread and put it doubled between two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you skillfully reach a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again to the part where you began, and pull your hand subtly and skillfully, until it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers, and assemble them, and wrap them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, then tighten it with another thread; it will remain and serve thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the straightening of the two healthy teeth, and of the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, then one puts it back in its place, freshly, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes one makes a tooth-shaped form from cow bone, and one puts it in the place where it is missing, and one tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves thus a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the frenulum of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this frenulum which comes from under the tongue is natural, one is born with it; or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is such that you open the patient's mouth, and have his head in your lap, and lift his tongue; then cut the nervous frenulum widely, until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, and this is from a sudden wound, then put in the hook and cut widely that ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, then bathe the place with rose water and vinegar, or with cold water, then put under the tongue a linen tent; and let the patient keep it there every night, that the place may not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if excessive bleeding occurs, then put crushed vitriol on the place; and if the bleeding overcomes you, then cauterize it with a lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of a livid color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is inclined to become a boil, and there is moisture, then throw in the hook, and incise it with a fine spatula, and free it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding overcomes you in your work, then put on crushed vitriol until it is stopped, then return to your work until you remove all the pus; then bathe the place with vinegar and salt, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come in the throat swellings which are called "goiter", and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then take heed: if it is a hard abscess of little feeling and livid color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also because of the excessive bleeding; but leave it until it is ripe, and then you will open it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a round white color, and the root is small, then have the instrument prepared for cutting, but first see if the heated abscess rests and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and he opens his mouth and the assistant takes it between his hands, and presses the tongue downwards with the instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and insert it into the tonsil, and pull it upwards as much as you can; and draw out some of the membranes with it, then cut it with the instrument, of which this is the form, that resembles small forceps; and however the points are curved, and one towards the other, and are very sharp, and is made of Indian iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then cut it with pincers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision let the patient gargle with warm water, and water and vinegar, and if excessive bleeding occurs, let the patient gargle with water, in which pomegranate bark has been boiled, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, then cut them as the two tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess which had grown in her throat, that is to say, one small abscess; and it had almost entirely closed the throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so much that it had forced out two nostrils through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and inserted a hook in one, then drew it out, and drew out a large portion of matter; then I did likewise in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the hook into this abscess, and cut a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was opened, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again constantly, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I incised it and cauterized it in the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When catarrh descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round below, it is called "uvula".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the heat of the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you must cut it; and that which is round and gathered and not long; and it is sanguine or of a dark color or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before; then insert the oncine into the uvula, and draw it downwards, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, you injure the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears the cutting, then you must use a device for cauterizing it without fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cautery is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient should put his head in your lap, and then press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and cauterize with hot, clear water, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use the end of this instrument, of which here is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should have on the head a cavity where one puts the medicine, like the bowl of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the uvula; and the patient should lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth and the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and injure it; then hold your hand with all the medicine and press it on the uvula, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it shrivel and the burning of the medicine is calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton in the throat above, until the cotton burns on the uvula; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and it will fall after four or five days. And if you need to start the cauterization with the medicine again, then restart it, and after the cauterization wipe around the uvula with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and be treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, or than cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamint, hyssop, origanum, rue, chamomile,  avens, and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and put vinegar in it, and bring it to a boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be a hollow instrument in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the ends be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the throat, until the uvula is mortified; afterwards, repeat it often, until the uvula dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things happen there; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a tube and put inside the end an eggshell, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and this is a good and healthy treatment.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fishbone, or something else, gets stuck in the throat; it is necessary then that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue down with an instrument, so that you can move the thing; and what is not visible to you and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the stuck thing will come out through vomiting; or let the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take a lead instrument of this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end raised; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest a cough comes, nor push the bone inside; and it is better that the patient inserts the instrument, so that he knows where the thing is lodged; so he pushes it down, or pulls it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is medicated, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when that does not help, then look in the patient's throat in the sunlight, after you press down the tongue with the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a horsehair, and put it in the patient's throat, then put a hot iron on the end of the hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient drink water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the leech feels the water, it falls out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I described in the fumigation of the uvula; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and the pot is covered with a cover pierced in the middle, and in that hole is the end of the instrument; then throw your fumigation in, and the patient puts the end of the tube in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes down to the leech; and the leech will fall immediately, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and astringent things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out forcefully by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one pulls out the leech is, when one can see it, similar to curved forceps to easily enter the throat; and it resembles a bird's beak, and has a rough surface like a file, so that what it grabs, it cannot let go; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses exist, according to what the memory brings forth here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and in size; and there are two ways, one being in its very appearance, and what it contains of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is according to the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own judgment in treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses which one should not pierce until the swelling is ripe according to its completion; and there are some that it is necessary to pierce when they are raw, and do not ripen according to their completion, such as abscesses which are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess occurs near the joints, and it is left until it is rotten around, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is near the principal member, and you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or if it is near the fundament, one pierces it before it is ripe; and it is not necessary that you pierce a raw abscess without completed digestion, except that which is near the fundament, lest it rot deeply, and become elongated inside, and a fistula form; and it cannot heal in a great time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to its completion, and that is when the pain is subsided, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the throbbing and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation sit in the most dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears most prominent; and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all similar places where there is no danger.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, along that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you delay the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the venom will be elongated from it, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And there are some abscesses that are pierced along the breadth of the body, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small holes in small abscesses; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many fissures according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut the core and cut it; when it has become like a rag and is dead, it is necessary to do as one does with buboes: and there are some that are split into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses of the angles; and there are some where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those which have no head, such as a smooth superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and it is necessary that when the abscess is large, and it has collected a great quantity of pus, and you pierce it, you do not draw out all the pus at that time, but you draw out a part; then you stuff the abscess until the next day, then you draw out some more; do this many times gradually, until all the pus comes out; especially if the patient is of weak constitution, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps out with the discharge of the pus, so that perhaps the patient dies, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, perform this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, apply linen or old cotton tents; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many holes, it is necessary that you place a tent in each one so that they meet each other; and if you have cut a part of the skin in the abscess, and you have cut around it, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or linen shavings without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth, and apply it to the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply the treatment and remedies, and the powders that I have mentioned elsewhere in this book, and if it is winter, and the area where the abscess is is very nervous, it is necessary that you apply tents and cloths moistened in warm wine and oil; and if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, it is necessary that you apply cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and clean and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the scalp small abscesses appear, and there are kinds that are in clusters, like the comb of a hen, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fatty ones and those with moisture like pus; and there are those that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not interfere.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of incision is such that you should test with the instrument which is called "entromissoire", whose form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then pierce it from above lengthwise.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, scrape it without leaving anything of the skin that contains that moisture, for it always returns when one leaves something there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this will drain what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains of the night; then treat the wound with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains thick pus, cut it lengthwise according to this form; and pour in your ointments, and scrape it on all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the abscess if it is stony, in cutting and cleaning it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the stony and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there are some of these abscesses on the head where there is no moisture, and of these was the abscess that I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and I could not break it; and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses appearing on the head, except for those that come at the temples of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, so that the pus may exit; and treat them as is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are many, and are intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own sheath, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to yield to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one then which you see of good disposition to the touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves on every side and is not close to the nerves of the neck or to the artery or to the duct, and is not deep; then you must cut it from above, and scrape it from each part, and stretch the two lips of the wound with hooks, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw it out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and that the spatula is not sharp or cutting, so that the hand does not slip, and does not go too far, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and that does not allow you to work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that stop blood, and tighten the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, return to your work, until you complete it; then seek with your index finger if there remain any small scrofulas, and cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, then you must not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all the scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and sew them immediately, since there is no superfluity remaining because of the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	then you must attend to cutting its root, and pulling it out forcefully, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas which contain superfluity, pierce them where they appear ripe; and pierce them in the same way as the aforementioned, hanging down, then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it consumes what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with flesh-generating ointment, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have quinsy, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be avoided; and that no help be given by this, because all the veins and the lungs of the patient are near to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it below the third or fourth ring, a small cut across, between the two rings or by the amount of the incision of the tonsil, not in the cartilage; and this place is so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh there, and the vessels are far away.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat with the finger, then cut the skin until he reaches the channel; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the tonsil, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the discharge of phlegm from the channel which spurts forth through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is feared, bring together the two lips of the wound in the skin, and sew it alone without the cartilage; then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely obstructed, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then the epiglottis is cut so that the patient can breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the malignancy of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. And then they ordered to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife, and plunged it into her throat, and cut part of the channels of the lung; and I was called to treat her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood which had flowed from it, and I knew well that she had not cut a vein or a conduit other than the throat, and the wind came forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that she was hoarse, and afterwards returned to her normal state; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and is a large abscess the color of a yellow yolk, and it is very common in women; and it is of two kinds: natural, and accidental; the natural kind has no remedy.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is of two sorts, of which one is similar to a fatty tumor, and the other kind is similar to an abscess which comes from an artery; and there is fear, and one should not operate with fire except in the case of one which is small, and prove and search it with the whole finger: if you find it like a nut of fat, and it does not adhere to any vein, then cut it, as one cuts nuts, and draw it out with its covering, if there is any; and search well all around, and treat it as is necessary, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the tumors
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many kinds of tumors, of which I will describe all the appearances; and now it is necessary that I describe all the difference which is between a tumor and a fistula.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a fistula is accompanied by heat and fever, until the boiling is past, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a tumor there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains a cyst, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and it begins like a swelling, and becomes large; and they are of two appearances, either fatty or moist, and many are of the color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the tumor, that you first examine and inquire with the instrument which is called "introducer," according to what its form will be in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the examination of abscesses of tumors is that you take the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then that it may be according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the introducer, and take care in what manner pus flows.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture comes out, whatever color it may be, treat it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the introducer no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, then incise it in a cross, and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape it from each side and guard the sac in which it lies so that you draw it out whole with the tumor; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the tumor returns many times; and if a little remains, and the blood troubles you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, and cleanse the wound, and apply things that soothe a hot abscess, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, then sew the two lips of the wound, and treat it with that which generates flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the throbbing vein is contrary to you or other things hasten you, and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it there two or three days, until the wound festers, and the boiling of the blood subsides; then return to cut away what remains of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the introducer instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three square ones which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, for encircling abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one sews wounds, and they are of yellow brass, or of iron, or of silver, and those which are yellow are worth more, and they are more proven of black lead for encircling the curves of fistula; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the hooks are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks which have two curves of three kinds also; and there are hooks which have three curves, and they are also of three kinds; and there are hooks which have two curves, and hooks of only one curve, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of those with which one cuts are sharp, and there are some which do not cut except on one side, with which one scrapes away tumors, so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and of these introducers, the blades are enclosed in handles, so that the patient does not feel them in the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy places, such as legs, and arms, and breasts, and in the groins, and in similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, similar to a small pruning knife, according to this form, with which one stops blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed in the place which is healthy to cut veins and arteries, and sometimes round according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must lance them according to this form from this line .b. down to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape away the fat, and fill the wound with flesh-generating medicine, then bring together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down, and is softened by its size as happens in women, then cut it in two sections above, by two similar incisions; of which one should meet the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply there what we have said of sutures and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it eats away the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are kinds of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those then which contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
