And the sign is, when it is from the section of the diaphragm, that it causes at the beginning a sudden pain, and the abscess is variously apparent, under the skin nearby, and this is because of the protrusion of the intestine and the body outside of the diaphragm.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the intestine, and are held there, and cause the patient to suffer great pain, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron there is fear, wherefore it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is that you instruct the patient to push the intestine back into the wound with his hand, if he can return it; then let it be supported on its neck, between your hands, and raise the thighs; then extend the scrotum upwards, and cut all the skin of the scrotum lengthwise; then insert into the lips of the wound hooks according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the egg can come out; then scrape the diaphragm which is under the skin of the scrotum, until the hard white diaphragm is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into that which surrounds the testicle, into that which is between the white diaphragm which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second diaphragm, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second diaphragm; and then move your right hand into the scrotum, and extend the white diaphragm upwards with your left hand, and raise the egg with all the diaphragm towards the groin; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and loosen that which is behind the ligature; and search with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped in the hard white diaphragm, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen below; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and put it into the back part of the diaphragm, which is behind the skin of the scrotum; after the groin, then cut the ends of the threads, until there are four threads; then assemble them one over the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the diaphragm, of which we have spoken, which is under the skin of the scrotum, with a strong ligature in two parts; then wrap the ends of the threads, and tie them firmly in two parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter into them, lest an abscess should form there; and again place the ligature according to the first ligature along two fingers of that, and after these two ligatures leave of the diaphragm which is under the scrotum the width of a finger; and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part which is under the skin of the scrotum, until the blood flows, and the bowel, as we have said before; then apply wool moistened in oil, and put it in the wound, and apply the ligature that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white diaphragm that we have mentioned is cauterized, after the incision, for fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling off, let it be sprinkled with warm water, and apply what we have mentioned, until it falls off; then treat the wound with other treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of fleshy hernia.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is done like the branch that is next to the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting above or slightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess with what works, until the vessels fall off; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and the place opens; and none of the intestines descend into the scrotum, and if some descend, it is little, and it returns every hour; and yet if it remains too long in this state, the wound or hernia increases, until the intestines descend; and this happens because of the extension of the hernia that is in the groin, as we have said, for it is extended, then the place softens and swells and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen place of the rupture lengthwise to the extent of three fingers; and then extract the hernia that is under the skin that follows it, then take a root and put it on the apparent place of the hernia; and press it deep into the belly, then sew the two apparent places of the hernia over the head of the root, and sew one and the other; then extract the head of the root, and do not cut the hernia nor stretch the egg or anything else, as I have shown you in the treatment of the intestinal hernia; then cure it by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The hernia is constricted, and there is no appearance of it in the rupture, and cautery is milder in this place, and closer to salvation (healing).
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the scrotum skin.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum is softened in some men, because the flesh within is softened, and it is ugly to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and cuts the softened skin above the natural skin; then bring the two edges together with a suture, and if you wish, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and the thread is removed.
dou chastrement	Of the castration.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary to know about it for two reasons: one is that the physician should know how to answer when asked about it, and know its treatment; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by traction, we make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then you take them in your hand until they are removed and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration by incision: you must hold the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament, and cut each testicle with one cut, once you have properly skinned them; and leave some of the tunica albuginea and the thin membrane that is over the vessels; and this method of castration is better than that which is done by traction, because in traction, by chance, some part of the testicles remains, which causes the animal to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is of two kinds in men: one is that between the two testicles appears something like the figure of a woman's nature, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other kind is in women, and they have above the vulva something like a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure for the man and the woman is that you cut away all the added flesh, and treat them like other wounds; in the second kind, of men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the headache.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tentigine is a growth on the natural part, so that it is very ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you grasp the excess of the tentigine with your hand or with forceps, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest excessive bleeding occur, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and there is another growth that arises at the opening of the womb, and fills it, and sometimes bursts forth, and is like a cauliflower, and for this reason the ancients called it "cauliflower disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we have said of the tentigine, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of wandering (disease/pain).
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the woman's nature is not pierced, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by a disease that has occurred; or it is by an added growth, or by a thin or thick membrane, and it is formed deep within the womb, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having menstrual flow; and knowledge of this is by the examination of the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is nearby and apparent, seek it with your fingers or with a probe.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a thin membrane, and it is near the labia, hurry, and break it thus: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, her legs spread; then spread the labia widely, until the thin membrane is broken, and the swelling is opened; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and put it on the place, and let the woman have intercourse every day, so that it cannot close.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the membrane is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of fleshy growth, suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have styptic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then apply a wide lead plate so that the wound cannot close; and let it be this way for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a fleshy growth appears in the vulva, it must be cut in this manner, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess which is in the vulva, one should not touch with iron.
des emorroides	of the hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins from which blood frequently flows, and when hemorrhoids are old they become swollen; and we have already mentioned in the division their similarities, and the signs, and I will now describe those that receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and swelling, when they are deep in the vulva, and are not apparent to the touch, are not treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the vulva, that one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Then you must place the woman in a cold room, then stretch the swelling with forceps, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that staunch blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and oak galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster of it for her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without wounding; then take wool, and moisten it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be cut as I have described the swelling; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the abscesses of the sea.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the sea, such as cancer and stony abscess and herpes and esthiomene and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary, then, that I discuss in this treatise the hot abscess which occurs in the sea, which is not one of the abscesses which gather pus; and if you wish to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let it mature until the pain is subsided; and then have the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he leans, and rests on his back and brings his feet together at the outer parts of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good bandage; then suck the pus towards the right side, and apply the instrument with which one opens the mouth of the fistula, of which the form will follow; and it is necessary that when you apply this instrument, that you first insert a probe to know the depth of the fistula, so that that which enters the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and that it does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the fistula with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument on top, and that he holds the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one opens it with a soft hand, then it is necessary to cut it at the head, at the spatula; and when the pus is emptied, then it is necessary that you put into the wound tents soaked in rose oil, or in dry verdigris oil; and put the tent outside the wound to the depth of the fistula, and put on the outside of the fistula and on the wound clean wool moistened in water in which mallows have been cooked; then cure it after two days with an ointment suitable for this, until it is healed; and sometimes one cleans the fistula and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then with water in which lily roots and long birthwort have been cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is deep in the fistula, then it is necessary that you avoid the cautery of iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is first necessary for the midwife that she knows the form of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downwards, and desires to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural form, and the issue is under its head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out quickly; for when it descends on its head, the afterbirth comes out with it, and the womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes on its feet, and the body or the head and hands come out first, or it comes on its belly, or sideways, and is perhaps turned over on its neck, and by other bad positions; it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the positions how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes head-first in the natural position, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a chair, or let the women hold her; and anoint her vulva with oil in which fenugreek has been cooked, and then let the midwife put between her fingers the small spatula of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and she splits the afterbirth, and cuts with her nail until the moisture which is inside flows out; and she presses the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek mucilage with linseed oil; then make her sneeze with hellebore, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will come out immediately.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out first, it is necessary that you gently put them back little by little; and if they cannot be put back, then place the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up; then push the seat to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall when you push; and if the hands cannot be put back, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife which is mentioned above, and extract the child, and reposition it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out feet first, it is necessary to push it upwards; and then turn it little by little, until it is straight; then take one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it comes down to the thighs, instruct her to strain, and make her sneeze with hellebore; then it will come out, if God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it comes out easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take mallow poultice, and oil of linseed, and melted gum, and grind everything together in a mortar; and apply this ointment inside and outside the woman's genitals, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened below, make her a pessary of myrrh, and place it inside, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and press her belly gently, for the child will come out immediately.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child onto her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this way, the midwife should put her hands on it little by little; then let it be supported by its neck, and its feet hanging down, and lying on a bed; and bend its hands little by little, and then take its hands above its belly, and remove the pillows from below, until it is positioned downwards; and if the child does not come out, then take its feet and move them forcefully, then move its belly upwards, then put your hands there; and draw the child out little by little; and instruct the woman to strain until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the delivery of the child that comes from the womb with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, make her lie down on a bed, and spread her legs forcefully; then administer the poultice that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on a seat, then try to bring back the hand; and draw the child out according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to strain until the child comes out completely.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the delivery of the child by its neck, with its arms outstretched, and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the midwife hold its hand, then turn it little by little, and draw it gently; and when it is straight, apply to the natural place a poultice of mallow and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a seat, and instruct her to strain; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner with the entire afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this manner with the entire afterbirth, cut the afterbirth with your nail, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child hangs by its face and neck, cut it at the navel so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to strain several times: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are a strange thing, and they do not live, except rarely; I know that they are multiplied, and are separated by the membrane that divides them, which is attached to the navel; and sometimes they issue as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue with difficulty, treat them as we have said, and let the midwife be skillful, and do quickly and easily what she does; and do so as it is best for salvation.
de plusors enfans	Of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the midwife know all this, for by chance such things happen to her; so let her do according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to use your hands; then you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman must be placed on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the attendant should hold her from two sides, or she should be tied to the bed so that she is not pulled down by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mucilage of mallow and fenugreek and linseed, then let the midwife oil her hands with these oils and mucilages; then put them into the womb gently, then look for a place where she can put her fingers that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is positioned so that it descends head first; then insert her fingers into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the groin or near the sides, and if the descent is feet first, then insert them into the heel and middle ribs; and she must hold the finger with her right hand, and place the curvature between the fingers of her left hand, and gently insert it with her whole hand, and insert her finger in any of these places that we have mentioned, until it reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another finger, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then extend them evenly, moving from one side to the other, to loosen it, and let the fingers be toothed to hold it, as is the form here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, let the midwife oil some of her fingers, and put them in that part, and pull out the other part; and if some still remains, then she puts this finger in a higher place, and does this until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back because of the tightness, then you must wrap it in a cloth, until it all comes out; then cut it at the joint of the palm or at the wrist, and so you must do with the other hand, and with the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the passage is narrow, or if there is an accumulation of water on the head, then you must put a spatumile espinous between your fingers, and split the head and drain the water; or you can break it with the instrument called "almidach", the form of which comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and do the same if the child naturally has a large head; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head comes out and is pulled at the groin, let it be split, until the moisture that is in the worst place comes out; and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the extraction is easy, and its placement at the mother's mouth is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or chest, then you must extract it with a cloth wrapped around the hand; and split the belly or chest, until the moisture that is there runs out; and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, then the midwife puts her hand deep into the mother, and pulls it down to the mother's mouth; then she puts one or two fingers in, and pulls it out; and if the mother's mouth is constricted by a hot abscess that has formed there, then you must not work there, but must administer moist and greasy things; and administer plasters, and sit in softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can place it evenly, then administer what we have said for a living child; and if one has no power, then pull it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, then administer what we have said for hot abscesses that occur in the mother; and if bleeding occurs, then she should be placed in astringent water, and other treatments should be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb a dead child had been, then another was conceived upon that one, and the other was also stillborn.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her groin, and it swelled until it opened, and began to greatly fester.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I considered it for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and a bone came out, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I wondered greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cleaned the wound, and extracted more bones, until the woman was in better condition; and the woman lived a long time like this, and a little pus always came from the place; and I have recounted this chapter only because when the master finds something strange, he should know how to give aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	of bringing the shoulder back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of the pressor, with which one uses the books; and with two turnings at the two heads of the two straps.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft should be one finger wide, and the edge of the branches one finger, and one and a half palms long; and between the two straps should be two additions of this same shaft, which are fastened at one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the shoulder to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, in the likeness of tongs; and it should have at the two ends two additions, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you want to open the shoulder with the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down and her legs open, then put the two additions joined together into the shoulder, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then open your hand with the instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the amount that you want to open the mouth of the shoulder, until the opening does what it should.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all surpassed, and their forms are multiplied; and when the physician has prepared them, the work is so much faster, and higher for men because of their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained after childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with a potion, and squeeze her hands on her mouth and nose; and if she expels it thus, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be boiled in the pot in water over the fire; then put one end of a tube in the hole of the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the womb, and hold it until the vapors enter the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the afterbirth will quickly be expelled.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand in olive oil or in mallow poultice, and then insert it into the vagina, and search for the afterbirth; and when she has found it, she should take it and gently pull it out straight, so that the womb does not tear during extraction; but she should move it slightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; then it will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is very constricted, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing, and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not come out with all that we have said, be careful not to force the extraction; but whatever is at the mouth of the womb, you should tie it to the woman's thigh, then administer a clyster of tetrapharmacon ointment; this will soften and relax it, and it will come out; however, when it softens, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary: some of the ancients have tested fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of the lochia and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass, similar to a funnel, and one inserts the narrow end into the vagina, and the wide end over the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and burn it until it is consumed, and begin again with another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the rectum.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the rectum pierced, but it is obstructed by a thin membrane:  it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a sharp instrument, and carefully avoid touching the wound; then apply wool soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close again, place a lead tube in the opening, and leave it for several days, and it should be removed when the child wants to defecate.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this obstruction comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cut that obstruction: and it should be treated, as we have said of the lead tube.
de la fistule dou fondement	Of the fistula of the rectum.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the rectum are a knotting and swelling that comes near the rectum externally, or in the space between the two parts; there is one fistula or several; and when this knotting is old, it works, and often white or thin pus discharges, and sometimes these fistulas are perforating; and they are known by the fact that there is an excretion or flatulence when the patient defecates, and sometimes a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the anus.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the perforating fistula of the rectum, and the non-perforating: and it is that you insert your index finger into the rectum, and insert a thin needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a thin lead probe, or a horsehair, until you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no excretion, flatulence, or worm coming from the opening, as we have said: know that it does not perforate; then hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is perforating to the bladder or to the urinary duct, urine comes out of it, and it cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced to the joint of the thigh, the probe reaches to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the location of the pain is around it, it is that there is always pus coming out of it, and neither medicine nor healing by ointment helps; and in these perforating fistulas there is no cure but labor, and the vanity of foolish doctors who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not perforating and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands; and raise his legs up to his thighs, and have his thighs bent towards his belly; then insert a bronze probe, or a lead one if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must put your index finger there, if you then feel that the probe has pierced it; and if it is discovered where you feel between your finger the pus or flesh, then know that it is perforating; then do not work on it, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	However, it is said that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the help that is done there is that the subtle cautery is heated according to the width of the fistula, as it is said above; and put it very hot into the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that these rotten parts are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then cure it with tents moistened in butter, until that rotten flesh comes out completely, then cure it with an ointment which engenders flesh and heals.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the probe enters, and does not pierce as far as the finger which is in the fundament, and there is between your finger and the probe a thick covering of flesh or pus, and you see the fistula at what follows the covering of the heart; then cut it from the beginning of the fistula, and keep putting the probe forward, and then the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the probe; and the probe will be delivered, and will fall; then cleanse those rotten parts which resemble a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood overcomes you, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery combines two good things: that is to say, the burning of these added parts, and the stanching of blood and the drying of moisture; then cure it with tents moistened in butter or in crushed herbs, until the place casts off pus, and the burnt flesh comes out completely in the pus; then cure the wound with healing ointments which generate firm flesh, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula goes as far as the bottom of the fundament, and is far from the body, put your finger in the fundament, and investigate it there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between the two is the membrane or the tissue or flesh, where it is about to pierce, there is no other way than trust and hope, by the administration of one of three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can, you put tents there and cure it as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the ligament which holds the fundament, and an evacuation occurs against the will; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse it once it is cut away from the fundament, either by tent or by other pointed instrument; then cleanse that corrupted flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound, and to confine the fistula to the part outside the fundament: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are in this manner: and it is when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is at the side of the fundament near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And put one twisted thread in two, and put the tent with the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is piercing through the margin of the fundament inwards, then draw the thread through that hole, so that you put your finger in the fundament; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two ends together, and pull one to the other, and leave it one or two days; and pull it sometimes, until the thread cuts the flesh that is between them, and they meet; then cure the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to cut so deep for the lacing, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatumile, a pointed instrument with which one opens the fistula, is very sharp on one side and cutting; and not on the other side, so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the rectum, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they constantly bleed, and there is one or more, and they are outside the rectum and at the end of the rectum; but those which are outside have little moisture, and constantly discharge a little clear water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the cure of those who have them inside the rectum is that you instruct the patient to strain to go to the privy, until the rectum protrudes, and the threads appear; then hurry, and seize it with forceps, or hold it with your nail, then cut it at its roots; and if the hooks cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle on some hot powders that are in place of a cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the rectum cannot protrude, then clysterize the patient with a biting and harsh clyster to wash what is in the rectum, so that it may come out clearly; when the patient strains, and the threads are outside the rectum, the cure is easy; and it is that you take them with your nail or with forceps, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and that he dreads the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must apply the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread above and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; and pull the thread tightly, then knot the thread, and remove the needle, and do so for all the others, and leave one to run off the excess blood; then put on the rectum a cloth moistened in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the rectum, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they fall off, and when they have fallen off, then cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the bile or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is dryness of bile in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is of no use.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you must scrape off the crust with the point of a spatula or your nail, so that it does not moisten; then cure it until it is healed as it should be; and if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the tremor
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formication is a small, false appearance around the body, and it goes very deep; and sometimes the cold finds it, and one feels it as if dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that quill on the tremor, until the circle encompasses the tremor entirely; then turn your hand with the entire quill until you cut around the tremor, and place it deep, and eradicate the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, do this with a silver or iron quill according to this form, and let it be thin below and thick above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	not pierced, to hold it with the finger, and press it. And if you wish, cauterize the tremor, as is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or tin, or molten or hammered bronze; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then which are administered in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large clyster is wider at the top, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a part where the belly is tied, as you see, and the end is pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other; and the belly where one puts the medicines is of an animal bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and has one finger's breadth between each hole, then put into these holes a strong thread of raw thread twisted in an X or around, and assemble the belly as is a goat's bladder; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; then let the minister squeeze it with both hands together, until it is completely empty, then withdraw the clyster, and let the patient raise his legs against the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it in as long as he can; and if he sleeps the whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize him for a disease of diarrhea, and the medicine hastens to come out, repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or an abscess, let the clyster be as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin clyster over which the leather is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatments by hand and by medicine, according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
