Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the throwing of stones, and the cutting of a sword and knife, or lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for the remainder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from the throwing of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless broken and the wound is large, and you fear the rising of a hot abscess: then make it bleed immediately from the cephalic vein, especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side from the injured part; and let the patient avoid repletion of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to bleed, let his food be lessened, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not exposed to the air, the powder that I will speak of a little later; and if the air has exposed it, then put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then bring them together by suture, as I will say in the wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is laid open to the bone, and hangs, and holds only by a little, then cut it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat heavy foods, such as bread and cooked wheat, also poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut away all the putrid part, and throw it away, then treat it; and if there is an artery or vein in the wound, from which blood flows, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then seek the artery, and if you find it loose, then tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder which heals before the air has exposed it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and powder it finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, unless it swells; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with quicklime alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but before the air has exposed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the air has exposed the wound, especially in summer, then one does not put this powder on it; but one puts on some digestive ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it throws off pus; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you later about head fractures.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one on the head, except if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything constricting on it, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be lukewarm, such as warm washings in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked herbs also washed in sweet water, and other minerals in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then pierce it in the lowest place; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, then open it, and wash it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the heart, and the passage is guarded, through which the food goes, then sew the heart to the throat bone, and do not touch the throat but restore it according to its natural shape; and then bind it carefully, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then search it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave them until the wound festers and the discharge is freed and cleaned; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound of lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then observe if the wound emits wind when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it because the blood may be retained deep within, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put on an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then no spasm will come, nor tremor, nor bad heart palpitations, nor difficulty of breathing; and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is safe.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it then with tents and other treatments, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and it festers, then know that there is a fistula; then treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether in the chest or on the back, treat it as that which is in front; if it is large, by suture; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is close to the bone, and has cut pieces of it, then cleanse the wound, and pull them out if they are separated; and if they are not separated, let the wound fester, so the extraction will be easier; and for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great, medium, and small; from the great wound, sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude, which causes the introduction of air; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is more difficult to put the intestines back in, unless one puts them back in immediately; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they go back in more with difficulty, and for that reason the medium wound is better, because one easily replaces the intestine in its place than the other two. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners: the two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the body and two other proper sutures are common to other wounds; and yet they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will describe each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine comes out, and it is difficult to put it back, this is by one of the two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or you boil in water squinant and cyprus and spike, and sprinkle the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes restraining wine does this, and is better than water alone to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, then moisten the intestine with water in which althea and mallows have been boiled, for by this the entry is easily made; and if it cannot enter, then slightly enlarge the wound with the instrument with which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than the incision, which one should not make without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting it: it cuts inside in the curve and not outside, and here is the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes, then put it back according to its natural form in its proper place, if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, then you must have the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then focus on ensuring that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say in large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, place what you have prepared, then have a compassionate assistant hold the entire rupture with his hand, and bring the edges together; and this is the common method of sutures, and it is that you take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound, then leave a finger's breadth from the edge of the wound, and insert a needle with a good strong thread; and pierce the two edges of the skin with the two edges of the siphac, which is beneath the skin inside, until you make it pierce that part, and bring together the two edges of the siphac, all four together; then twist a double thread around the needle from both sides, then bring the two edges of the wound together properly, and then leave a finger's breadth, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease doing this as you need needles, until the entire wound is closed; and the needles should be medium-sized, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter properly: therefore they must be medium-sized; and one must not thrust the needles too far outside of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the closure; and then cut the ends of the needles, so they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or cloths at the ends of the needles to hold them better, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of suturing with needles is more suitable in small wounds, because one or two needles suffice. The second suture is common, and is that you bring together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the siphac together with a needle with a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these four edges together, then bring the needle back to the part where you began, in the way that cloths are sewn; and leave a space between each stitch the width of a little finger; this suture the men use, and I sewed a wound that a man had in his belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and two palms of intestine protruded, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I put the intestine back after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed within fifteen days, and I treated it, and it was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none was found, nor any medicine; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and thrust it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced straight through, then leave the edge of the siphac where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside to the outside; and the meaning of this suture is that you sew as the furriers sew furs, and that you leave the siphac once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the suture is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen properly describes, is as some do, who bring the two parts together naturally, and apply one edge of the siphac to the other edge, in this manner: insert a needle in the edge of the mirach nearby, and make it pierce that place only, and leave the two edges of the siphac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside to the inside, at the two edges of the siphac; then make it pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, at two other edges of the mirach which are on the other side; and this is the easiest method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is the same as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the heat has changed it, you should immediately replace the intestine, and sew it; then put on a powder which generates flesh, and if the heat has changed it, put on any ointment that is at hand, until the wound heals; and cut the threads, and let the siphac and the mirach be joined; then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to discharge pus, old cotton, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound will communicate with the principal members, you must moisten light wool in oil of moderate warmth, or in rose oil, and put it around the groin, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or corruption in the bowels, and this often happens, then clysterize them with warm black wine, and especially if the corruption reaches the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, put it back in place like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become worm-eaten or black, you must tie the area that is black, so that no blood flows there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and let the two ends hang down from the part below the wound outwards to facilitate extraction when the intestine falls, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it became festered and developed a fistula, and the excrement and winds issued from it; I applied treatment according to my ability, and I did not cease to work until he was healed, and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I feared that the patient might have harm in his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some practitioners said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large-headed pins, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it over the two edges so that it grasps them; and then cut off its head, and this holds so that it cannot come undone, then place another pin afterwards in the same manner as before, until the whole wound is closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	These pins are inserted into the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is taken from the intestine of a beast, in this manner: take the end of this intestinal thread that is very cleaned, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and bring it back to the rupture; and this method of sewing with pins is not stronger than according to the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no device or certainty, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula," and especially when it is haired and produces pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is, in truth, a hard and white knotted swelling, where one feels no pain, and it is as hairy as a bird's feather; and sometimes clear pus comes from it, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, is only so for one of nine reasons: that is to say, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its bad quality; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the edges, which does not allow flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence; or because the property of the region is slow in digestion, and slow in healing, and swollen by nature; or because there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures by medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary that I make you know the cure of a fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for there are fistulas that occur in the large veins, and in the arteries, and in the nerves, or in the diaphragm, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in some joint of the hands or feet; and there are such that occur in the principal member, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but work and skill; and if there is any fistula that does not reach the places I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you wish to know it, then take a tent of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, and probe it; and if the fistula is crooked, search it with a thin lead tent, for lead bends easily around the tortuousness; and if the fistula has several openings and you cannot probe it well with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for the moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then probe it carefully as far as you can, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and if it is hairy deep down, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut it according to what I have told you, and remove the swelling and the corrupted flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, then you must cut deep, as much as you can, then put in tents soaked in medicinal water, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments that generate healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not hinder you in the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it until all the corruption is removed, then cure it with things that generate flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and pus returns as before, know that you have not gone to the bottom: then uncover and probe until you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature; and if there is a small piece of corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with tongs, then remove it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, and do not leave even one; and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no danger or fear, then cut both moisture and flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them at once, then apply something that generates putrefaction to the wound, and leave it until the place is putrefied around the bones, and then the bones will come away more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then scrape only the corruption until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the bone corrupted, and it reaches the marrow of the bone; then it must be sawn and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example from it and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause for it to open; but the physicians, through their folly, worked on it so much that the abscess opened, and much matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many openings appeared, which all discharged pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art present, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which it was treated, and what flowed from the openings in great quantity; and the skin of the young man became red, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I inserted a tent into one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that one came towards the others from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the openings until I uncovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupt and perforated, and the corruption went to the bone inside; I sawn what appeared to me of the corrupt bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except that which I removed; and I began to restore the wound with cleansing medicines for a long time, and it could not heal; and then I recommenced, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I sawn it, and then removed it, and I tried to heal the place; but I could not, until I cut around a palm's breadth of the bone, and removed it completely with its marrow, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and healed quickly, and it was not necessary to recommence the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation he bled often, but he was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew firm flesh, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary at all, neither in walking nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it must be sawn in this manner: take a linen thread, and tie it to the end of the bone which is visible, and instruct someone to pull it upwards; and place another linen thread, thicker than the first, and tie it above the flesh which is over the bone, and stretch the end, so that you pull the corrupt flesh downwards, and uncover the flesh over the place where you wish to saw, so that the saw does not wound the flesh; and place a fire-coal or a small board under the bone in order to move and cut the corrupt flesh; and it is necessary to saw as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and saw again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupt, and does not appear, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a fire-coal underneath, and then saw from one part to the other the corruption, and let the sawing of the length of the corruption be a little, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupt joint, and saw the bone where it continues on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the ankle of the foot, then this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless it is necessary that you examine this corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not hinder you; and know that the incisions and the saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and their thinness, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument of which you will have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the kinds of illnesses; so prepare the instrument which you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The flesh rots either from an internal cause or from an external cause; and when you have medicated this corrosion by the cure of medicines, and they do not help, then it is necessary to cut that member as far as the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes death by this means, or the greater harm, of the loss of the member; and the sign is that the member becomes black, so that it seems that it is burned by fire, and rots after the blackness, then that corrosion goes from member to member, and takes over the whole body; so hasten to cut, and if it is by the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and the like, if the corrosion is at the tip of the finger, cut it off, and do not give it space to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut it off at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut it off at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedies avail except the quantity of its virtue; and do likewise when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it off after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it goes up into the leg, cut it off at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the member is that you tie it above and below, and one assistant stretches one of the threads downwards, and another assistant the other thread upwards, and you separate the flesh which is between the two threads to the width of a span, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or saw it, and put on each side a linen cloth, so that the saw does not touch the healthy place, and another lesion and hot abscess comes to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the place immediately, or put on some styptic powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: a blackness came upon him which resembled a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came on his toe, until it seized the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off his foot, and was healed; and a long time afterwards the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me, and I put on him repercussive things after the cleansing of the body, and the corrosion could not cease; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I would not, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his own country, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have told this story only so that one may do likewise, if one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in fleshy places, and remains so long that it forms a large collection of pus; and then it breaks and bursts, and the pus leaps out, and the place remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin which is above is as thin as a fine cloth, and it does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone deeply, it is called "fistula"; and the cure is that you cut that skin all around, and especially when it is thin, like a cloth; and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are confident that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with a clyster thus: see if the abscess is large, and the pus that comes out is foul-smelling, then clysterize it with Egyptian medicine, which is made thus: take vinegar, oil, and litharge, equally, and put them to cook in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and put it in water and honey, and clysterize the abscess, and squeeze out the opening; and leave the medicine in for two hours, then squeeze it out; do this many times, until the abscess is cleansed, and the stench is removed; and sometimes it is clysterized with lye water, when this medicine is not present, and that is that you take ash from vine wood, and pour water over it, then strain it, and clysterize with it, until you know that the abscess is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the lye water, clysterize it with water and honey in which there is a little crushed litharge; or clysterize it with honey and medicated wine, the honey having the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the abscess heal; and when you have done this, and you are confident that the abscess is well cleansed, clysterize it with that which makes flesh grow in it, and that is that you take diaphinit plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or clysterize it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken of the properties in the treatise on ointments; and if the opening of the abscess is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, widen it a little with an iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, sew it and leave only a place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening which discharges pus is at the top, cut it in the lowest place that it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the abscess below as you wish, prepare in such a way that the pus runs to the lowest place that is there, for when the pus is deep, it does not allow flesh to grow; and if you cannot cut the abscess below as you wish, prepare in this way: that the pus runs easily downwards, and leave nothing of the pus; and take consolidative medicines to put on the abscess, and spread them on a linen cloth which covers all the abscess; then cut forcibly at the opening of the abscess a little wider than before, then spread soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and put it on the opening of the abscess to facilitate the discharge of pus, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and the one that is on the opening of the abscess, remove often to remove the pus, and know what comes out of the pus, whether it is venom, little or much, or digested, or undigested; and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine is spread in this manner and you see the nature which oozes from the opening of the abscess, know that the abscess will heal, and health approaches; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the abscess discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the abscess will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if thin venom flows after a long time, do not despair of healing, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose flesh is slow to grow in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested pus flows from the abscess after many days, know that the abscess will not heal; and if the abscess is slow to heal, and is prolonged, add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, for there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and rose of old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and this same thing cooked thicker does better, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and crush it, and powder it over the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue a cloth to it, and spread it over the abscess, and sometimes aristolochia longa is administered, and roots of white lily, which is like bean flour and centaury; and use it of simples or of compounds: crush them, and make powder of them, and put it over the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments; then cure it with the cure of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A whitlow is an abscess that arises under the nail of the little finger of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps arises in other fingers; and when it is old, and one does not take care of it, there comes a hot abscess, and it runs and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it corrupts it entirely; and the corrosion goes to the bone, until there comes a foul smell, and the head of the finger swells, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you cure it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, then you must cut away with iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to prick and wound it, then you must put a thin instrument under the nail that pricks the flesh, and lift it, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it and draw it out, for as long as the corrupted bone is there, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger corrupt, cut it at a joint as is said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is injured, and swollen, and feels great pain, then you must heal it first; then cut the nail with a sharp instrument by cutting across from above, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh that is under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the thumb of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The extra fingers that grow on the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there are some where there are bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and some of them grow at the root of the joint, or their origin is in some joint of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which grows in a joint of the finger does not move, and that which grows at the joint of the finger, by chance moves; the cutting of that which is fleshy is light, in this manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which grows at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:  hold yourself back from cutting it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which grows on the last joint of a finger, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a saw suitable for this, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining together that happens to fingers comes from birth, or from the closing of a wound, or from a burn by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut that joining, so that the fingers return to their natural forms; then place between them tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not rejoin; or you place between them thin pieces of lead, until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a joining occurs to any of the fingers with the palm, cut that joining as necessary.
des vils	of the vile things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Varices are large swollen veins full of melancholic superfluities, which appear in many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk on foot and who work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then it is necessary that you administer a purging of bile, and then bleed from the basilica vein.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron [presumably referring to an injury caused by iron] is according to two methods: one is that one cuts them and draws out the black blood; and the other method is that you raise the vein and draw it entirely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first bathe the leg in very hot water until the thick blood is thinned, then bind the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or in two or in three, with a wide cut, then lift and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient's strength can bear; and then bind it, and instruct him to abstain from foods that generate black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The removal of it is according to this method: shave the patient's leg, if there is much hair, then put him in the bath, and bathe the leg in hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut to the vein along the length to the head of the knee, or in the part below at the ankle; then open the skin with an instrument, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when one feels it; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put a hook underneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then fasten it to a hook lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the hook, as you have done, and fasten it to another hook, as you did first; then cut another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it, and cut it at the toe, then draw it and lift it to the second incision; then draw it from incision to incision, until it comes out entirely, then cut it; and if you cannot draw it and lift it, put a needle with a strong double thread in it, and tie it and draw it, and put a hook underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, then it cannot be drawn or lifted, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put on the wound wool soaked in wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then it is necessary that you split it forcefully, but do not cut it; and draw it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and does not cut sharply, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of a thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but it should be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the superficial vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is generated in legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it is generated elsewhere than in legs, and this happens from the putrefaction that comes from under the skin, as serpents and worms come inside the body, generated between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.
